Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Obstructive sleep apnea is a disorder characterized by frequent episodes of partial or complete blockage of the upper airway during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a rare, benign tumor in the jawbone that may cause pain, swelling, and jaw stiffness, but not sleep apnea.
  Dentigerous cyst is an odontogenic cyst that develops from the follicle of the tooth germ and surrounds the crown of an unerupted tooth, but not related to sleep apnea.
  Orbital fracture is a break in one or more bones that form the eye socket, which may cause double vision, decreased vision, or swelling around the eye, but not obstructive sleep apnea.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joint is fixed and unable to move properly, and may cause difficulty chewing, speaking, or opening the mouth, but not sleep apnea.
  Therefore, none of the given options cause obstructive sleep apnea.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
Obstructive sleep apnea is a sleep disorder in which breathing is repeatedly interrupted during sleep. This happens when the muscles in the back of the throat fail to keep the airway open. 
Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst both are benign odontogenic tumors that develop in the jaws and do not affect the airway. 
An orbital fracture is when one or more bones around the eye are broken. 
Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw is completely or partially immobile because of fusion of the mandibular condyle to the base of the skull. This condition may cause obstruction to the airway and lead to obstructive sleep apnea.
Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.

Question: Most used selective medium for streptococcus rnutans is
Choices:
  A: Mac conkey medium
  B: Mitus salivarius bacitracin agar
  C: Nutrient agar
  D: Tellurite medium
Response 0:
Thought:
  Streptococcus mutans is a type of bacteria commonly found in the human mouth and is a significant contributor to tooth decay.
  It is a gram-positive, facultative anaerobe, and can grow on a variety of media.
  The selective medium is a type of culture medium that promotes the growth of the desired organism while inhibiting the growth of unwanted organisms.
  MacConkey medium is selective for gram-negative bacteria and contains bile salts and crystal violet.
  Mitus salivarius bacitracin agar is selective for Streptococcus mitis and Streptococcus salivarius, but not specifically for Streptococcus mutans.
  Nutrient agar is a general-purpose medium that can support the growth of many types of bacteria.
  Tellurite medium is an enriched medium used to isolate Corynebacterium diphtheriae, not Streptococcus mutans.
  Therefore, the most used selective medium for Streptococcus mutans is not listed in the options provided.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Streptococcus mutans is a gram-positive bacterium.
  Selective media are used to promote the growth of one group of organisms over another.
  MacConkey agar is a selective and differential medium for gram-negative bacteria.
  Nutrient agar is a general-purpose medium that supports the growth of most microorganisms.
  Tellurite medium is selective for Corynebacterium diphtheriae.
  Mitus Salivarius Bacitracin (MSB) is a selective medium used to isolate Streptococcus mutans from saliva.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Mitus Salivarius Bacitracin agar.

Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy is a dental procedure in which the entire pulp in the root canal is removed.
  Pulp capping is a dental procedure in which a medicament is placed over the exposed pulp to facilitate healing and formation of secondary dentine.
  Primary teeth are also known as deciduous teeth or baby teeth.
  Primary teeth have a shorter root compared to permanent teeth, and the apex is wider, which allows better access to the root canal.
  The pulp chamber in primary teeth is larger compared to permanent teeth.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth.
Action: Answer("C")

Thought: 
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are treatments for infected or damaged pulp.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that develop in children.
  Primary teeth have different properties than permanent teeth.
  The success of pulpectomy and pulp capping in primary teeth is due to a specific characteristic of primary teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity in the young is responsible for the better response to treatment.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")

Thought:
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are dental procedures on the pulp of the tooth.

Topic: Dental
Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:
  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Thought:
 Malocclusion is a condition where the teeth are not properly aligned when the jaws are closed.
 Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population who have a specific condition at a specific point in time.
 Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a condition in a population over a specific period of time.
 Morbidity is the state of being diseased or unhealthy within a population.

Question: Object permanence seen in which stage of Jean Piagets theory

  A: Sensorimotor
  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage

  Phosphocreatine is a molecule that can rapidly donate a phosphate group to ADP to synthesize ATP.

Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Proteinuria is a condition where an abnormal amount of protein is found in the urine.
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, most often the liver and kidneys.
  If preeclampsia is severe, it can be life-threatening for both the mother and the baby.
  Severe preeclampsia is usually diagnosed when a pregnant woman has a blood pressure of 160/110 mm Hg or higher, along with other symptoms such as proteinuria.
  The level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is usually 5 grams or more in a 24-hour urine collection or 3+ or higher on a urine dipstick test, which is equivalent to 300 mg or more of protein in a 24-hour urine sample.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 300 mg.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy-related disorder characterized by hypertension and proteinuria.
  Severe preeclampsia is a form of preeclampsia that is associated with complications such as eclampsia, HELLP syndrome, and acute renal failure.
  The diagnostic criteria for severe preeclampsia include systolic blood pressure >= 160 mmHg, diastolic blood pressure >= 110 mmHg, proteinuria >= 5 g/24 hours or >= 3+ on dipstick, and other features such as thrombocytopenia, impaired liver function, and pulmonary edema.
  The question asks for the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia. 
  The answer is D: 3000 mg (which is equivalent to 3 g).

Question: The patients with class II division 1 malocclusion have

  C: Hypertonic upper Lip
  D: Hypotonic upper lip

  Patients with Class II division 1 malocclusion have a convex profile, which means that their upper lip is more projected than the lower lip.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Hypertonic upper Lip.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Class II division 1 malocclusion is a type of malocclusion where the upper front teeth are positioned more forwardly in relation to the lower front teeth.
  Hypertonic means an increased muscle tone while hypotonic means decreased muscle tone.
  Patients with Class II division 1 malocclusion have a retruded mandible and an overjet.
  Overjet refers to the horizontal distance between the upper and lower incisors with the lower incisors positioned posteriorly to the upper incisors.
  The lower lip is affected by the position of the mandible.
  Therefore, the patients with Class II division 1 malocclusion have a hypotonic lower lip.
